Slake on the half-beat. Tempermark what you promise. Post it. The world isn’t healed. It’s held. That’s enough.\n________________\n\n\nChapter 1: Wet Trace at Blackgate\nBell Two rang short across the Underface. Jhace climbed the ladder out of the low heat, hand closing on rung, the metal sweating under his palm. He came up into Blackgate’s choke where the carts were backed nose to nose, and the Posting board glared white with its Tempermark pin and droplet icon.\nTiffani had already chalked a half-circle behind them so the crowd couldn’t press too close. She stood in the ring’s gap, one hand on her Veil case, the other tracing light against the stone seam. “Hold your tongue out of the way,” she said without looking. “It’s a quick one.”\nJhace set his pack down, rolled his sleeves, and touched the home ring bolted to the post. “One hand on home.”\nShe nodded, voice gone flat with routine. “One hand on home.”\nBrighlee arrived from the Conclave, still breathing through paper. “Work order nine-three-two. Wet Trace, Blackgate span. Setter Jhace brast, glass Tiffani veld, no hold.” She Tempermarked the droplet card, clipped it to the board, and stepped back. Tiffani’s eyes lingered on the ink longer than Brighlee’s hand—counting strokes, weighing silence. Names posted, Bell recorded. The carts quieted.\nThe note from the Chain said quick Vein under the gate plate—heat moving wrong, a shallow slip that could cut the cart path clean through the Underface if ignored. Persuasion before force. Always persuasion first.\nJhace unpacked what he needed: two wedges, seven-degree cut; copper-nib trace stick; bladder of wet. Nothing else. He checked his fray bands and the dull brass ring on his left wrist for crack. Sound.\n"

            "You built a working-class magic system out of civil engineering. It slaps. Now let’s cut the drag and sharpen the blade.\n\nfileciteturn0file0\n\n# What’s working (keep, amplify)\n- The rules-as-religion vibe is killer: “Trace wet. Wedge before Veil. One hand on home.” It’s a liturgy people can live or die by.\n- The craft porn sings. Tools, angles, beats, the smell of steam and resin. Feels earned, not cosplay.\n- Your recurring quartet (Jhace, Tiffani, Brighlee, Mel) gives the city a pulse. Interludes (Corlexi, Mobel) widen the lens without bloating the cast.\n\n# What’s dragging (fix now)\n- **Exposition density.** The prologue frontloads lore like a freight train. Great lines in there, but it’s 2–3x longer than its welcome. Readers will follow a mystery; they bail on a manual.\n- **Process repetition.** Many chapters resolve “arrive → wedge → trace → Slake → Veil → witness.” Reliable, but predictable. Stakes blur.\n- **POV drift.** Mostly tight third on Jhace/Tiffani, then occasional omniscient aphorisms that break the spell. Pick close third and stick the landing.\n- **Jargon opacity.** “Whitequench,” “Overbind,” “Tempermark,” “Shade skins” are tasty, but a few are introduced without immediate on-page consequence. If it’s important enough to name, it’s important enough to hurt someone.\n- **Antagonism is abstract.** Lonce & Parr and Crown techs are straw-villains right now. Give us a face (exec, inspector, saboteur) to punch or outsmart.\n\n# Fastest path to a sharper book\n1) **Prologue → 2 pages max.** Keep the lung metaphor, the Bore, the Veinwright creed, and the Bells. Cut the rest or push it into epigraphs before chapters as “posted rules.”  \n2) **Open on character, not cosmology.** Chapter 1 is already solid. Make the prologue a teaser; Chapter 1 becomes the true start.  \n3) **Escalate the job loop.** Every fix should either cost more, reveal new rot, or force a rule-break. No lateral wins.  \n4) **Show the forbidden.** Put **Overbind** and **Whitequench** on page once each. Controlled demo gone wrong. Real blood, real consequences.  \n5) **Name the foe.** Give Lonce & Parr a human (e.g., **Eddin Parr**, logistics czar with clean hands and dirty ledgers) and a Crown fixer who “consults” then bails. Make them smart.  \n6) **Consequences that stick.** Jhace’s hand, Tiffani’s fog-sickness, Mel’s witness fatigue. No magic resets. Let injuries change how they work.  \n7) **Interludes with knives.** Corlexi’s burn and Mobel’s audit are great. Each interlude should flip a lever that forces the next crisis, not just add flavor.\n\n# Structure pass (one-page outline)\n- **Act I (Set the rules, break one):** Blackgate, Strathmoor, Lowcourt establish method and team. End Act I with **Narrowvale HALT** where they must violate a posted rule to save the arch. Policy backlash begins.\n- **Act II (Systems bite back):** Heat Splice under Alderline exposes L/P bad lots; Double Fault at Rindle Yard forces precedent. Interlude: Mobel melts forged weights; the ban on shop trace lands. Midpoint: **public collapse narrowly averted** because Mel refuses to sign without proof, calling their bluff.  \n- **Act IIb (Pressure + sabotage):** Thirteen Corners sequence becomes a rolling set piece with a time cap. Reveal: L/P’s “storage error” is an active reroute of feed temps to sell more skins.  \n- **Act III (Hold or break):** City leans toward the Bore after a Crown overbind. Team orchestrates a citywide counterbend using bells and posted rules as a literal score. Victory is measured, not shiny: “The world isn’t healed. It’s held.”\n\n# POV hygiene\n- Lock to **close third** per scene. No sudden omniscient flare-ups. Keep aphorisms in posted-rule epigraphs so the voice stays diegetic.\n\n# Style sheet (make it consistent)\n- Caps: Bore, Bells, Vein(s), Veinwright(s), Conclave, Crown, Underface, Trace, Veil, Slake, Overbind, Whitequench, Tempermark, HALT.  \n- Tools/objects lower: wedges, shade skins (but “Shade 1/2” is capped as grade), copper nib, Lume.  \n- Mantras italicized on first use in a scene; not every time.  \n- Time: always with Bell counts and absolute hour only when relevant.\n\n# World terms that need a bruise on-page\n- **Whitequench:** show a piece of glass or skin that rings bright then shatters later, cutting a kid’s boot.  \n- **Overbind:** demonstrate why “a clean disaster still kills you.” A bridge that holds perfectly until a temperature swing, then fails catastrophically.  \n- **Tempermark:** have a forged one fail mid-crowd. Panic. Lesson learned in public.\n\n# Pacing tune-ups per chapter\n- **Prologue:** compress; move “One hand on the home ring” into Chapter 1’s header as a posted rule.  \n- **Ch1–4:** keep; tighten beats by 10–15% each. Let Tiffani land one mistake early so she’s not invincible.  \n- **Ch5 (Lockfall):** fantastic chaos; clarify spatial stakes with three landmarks so readers aren’t lost in the spray.  \n- **Interludes (Corlexi, Mobel):** each should end with a policy or symbol that tangibly changes the next chapter’s options.  \n- **Ch7 (Rindle):** mark the rule-break loudly on the board; seed future political fallout.  \n- **Ch8 (HALT):** make “consultation complete” from Crown techs a knife twist. Name one.  \n- **Ch11–12 (Veil recall / shop trace):** merge into one cascading scene that crescendos with a public ban announcement over the Bells.\n\n# Sample edits (surgical, not stylistic overwriting)\n**Prologue first para — tighten to punch:**\n> The world ended once and decided staying dead was too much work. The crust flexed like a lung after a punch. A straight pull tore a tunnel with no opposite mouth. We named it the Bore so the wound would pretend to be finished.\n\n**Lockfall clarity pass (shorten, anchor space):**\n> Water climbed Jhace’s ribs, warm and fast. Counterbrace stuck. Pin half-seen. He braced a knee, drove the wrench. Teeth jumped. Metal screamed. “Cut the feed!” Tiffani. “Valve’s jammed!” Brighlee. Hammer. Crack. Gate slid an inch. Vein bit hard under the plate. Wet trace, half-beat Slake. The gate took weight and the water stopped trying to climb his throat.\n\n# Character arcs (give them dents)\n- **Jhace:** craftsman ethic vs. body limits. His hand forces him to adapt technique, train a junior, delegate, hate it, and do it anyway.  \n- **Tiffani:** perfectionist glass-sense vs. necessary shortcuts. She must authorize a fix she can’t personally witness.  \n- **Mel Quarr:** incorruptible witness vs. triage math. She signs one repair she can’t fully prove and lives with it.  \n- **Brighlee:** clerk to commander. The ledger starts running the city because she posts faster than policy can catch up.\n\n# Title check\nYour current title works. Alternatives if you want sharper teeth:\n- **Stress Remembers**\n- **One Hand on Home**\n- **Trace Wet**\n- **Tempermark**\n- **The World Isn’t Healed, It’s Held**\n\n# Back-cover logline (usable now)\nWhen a city built over a one-mouthed abyss starts to shift, a crew of Veinwrights who negotiate with stress and heat must break their own posted rules to keep bridges breathing, while a supplier’s quiet sabotage turns safety into theater and faith into math.\n\n# Punch-list (do these first)\n- Cut prologue to 600–800 words; move excess into epigraphs.  \n- Seed and on-page demo: Whitequench and Overbind.  \n- Consolidate Ch11–12 into a single recall-ban cascade with a human antagonist present.  \n- Add one named L/P antagonist and one Crown tech.  \n- Give Jhace a technique change after the burn; adjust at least two later scenes to reflect the new method.  \n- Mark all rule-breaks publicly on boards with consequences that echo 2–3 chapters later.\n\nIt’s already good. Trim the sermon, raise the cost, show the forbidden, and let the city remember what it owes you. Then you’ll have something readers press into friends’ hands like a warning and a promise."

It didn’t break apart; it flexed, like a lung taking air after being punched. A pull went through the crust—straight, fast, absolute—and stopped just short of tearing clean through. What it left was a tunnel with no opposite mouth. People called it the Bore, because naming the wound makes it sound finished.  \n[L4] From the Upper Crown, it looks like an even circle of shadow on maps. From the Underface, it’s a black horizon that presses in your teeth when the air gets heavy. Nobody pretends it’s a mystery anymore. We live around it, not above it. Every crack, every bridge, every load-bearing inch answers to what the Bore changed.  \n[L5] It began with water taking new routes. Rivers turned, cliffs sagged, docks listed without warning. For a year the wind came up from the ground instead of the sky, and you could smell iron on your skin no matter how often you washed. People called it divine; the rest of us called it gravity. When the air stopped shaking, a handful of us were still standing, and we started measuring before we started praying.  \n[L6] We found the veins by accident. They ran under the ground like nerves under skin, thin lines where force preferred to travel. When the veins slipped out of their old paths, they bled heat and pressure and made Harrow—the kind of rupture that doesn’t care if you’re watching. A few people, tired of being erased, learned to touch the veins and guide them. Those hands became Veinwrights. Their work became the city’s language: Trace. Set. Bridge. Veil. Slake. Tempermark.  \n[L7] The Bore taught one rule that never stopped mattering: everything carries stress, and stress remembers. You can’t erase a fault; you can only give it a safer way to move. That’s what the craft is—negotiation between material and will. Every building stands because someone convinced it not to fall.  \n[L8] Six months after the pull, the first bridges started breathing. At night you could see vapor lifting from the joints like ghost breath. No one remembers laying the mains that kept them warm, but the warmth stayed. It rose through basements and clinics, through pipes that had no valves, through the Conclave halls where the Veinwrights kept their ledgers. The city learned to live with the heat as a fact, not a gift. It kept people alive in winter, and it kept them honest—because if a line failed, everyone nearby heard it.  \n[L9] When the air cooled, the Bells came. Not temple chimes—work signals. Long clear rings for reopen, two short for brace, fast beats for Harrow risk. Each Bell came with a board stamped in copper and sealed in glass. You could tell a city’s health by how clean its Tempermarks were.  \n[L10] The first posted rule was ugly and perfect: One hand on the home ring. Hold something that won’t move while you touch what might. It was less philosophy, more survival.  \n[L11] Then came the rest, written by people who’d already bled once for the knowledge: — Trace wet. Dry lines please eyes and lie to Veins. — Wedge before Veil. Cool the draft, then the glass. — Half-beat Slake. — Countermark cooler than birth. Pride bends things wrong. — No White. — Brace taps only in Bells Two and Three. You are not special in Four.\n# 【1†The Line That Holds.txt†file_0000000056ec61f59aedbe23466069ae】\nContent source: Source.file\nTitle: The Line That Holds.txt\nCitation Marker: fileciteturn2file1\nMclick Target: \"2:1\"\nContent Snippet:\n[L1] ﻿Prologue — The Year the World Took a Breath\n[L2] The world ended once and decided it was too much trouble to stay dead. You could tell a city’s health by how clean its Tempermarks were.\n[L9] The first posted rule was ugly and perfect: One hand on the home ring. Hold something that won’t move while you touch what might. It was less philosophy, more survival.\n[L10] Then came the rest, written by people who’d already bled once for the knowledge: — Trace wet. They’re methods. Watch a street when a blue HALT goes up and every hammer stops midair. Watch the crowd hold breath until the setter witness signs the clear. That’s how cities stay alive—by honoring pause more than noise.\n[L2] We forbid Overbind, because a clean disaster still kills you. We forbid Whitequench, because a lie in glass cuts deeper than heat. We measure by what doesn’t fail, not by what shines.\n[L3] After the Bore, Bells multiplied. Every trade learned its rhythm. The Couriers’ Bell marked motion; the Conclave’s marked repair. You could walk a full day and never be out of hearing range. It was noise that meant survival—call, answer, repeat.\n[L4] Six hundred and twelve rounds later, Te’Oga still leans a fraction toward the Bore. Maps mark the tilt with a single diagonal line through the city’s name. Children in the Underface draw circles in ash to guess the next drift. Crown engineers add decimal places to comfort themselves. Neither side is wrong.\n[L5] The Bore doesn’t threaten anymore. It just exists. We’ve made a kind of peace with the wound: keep it measured, keep it known, keep it held.\n[L6] Work here isn’t sacred. It’s necessary. The Conclave says “Trace wet.” The Couriers answer, “One hand on home.” Together, they make the city stay where it is.\n[L7] If you need a prayer, you use your hands: Trace wet. Wedge before Veil. Slake on the half-beat. Tempermark what you promise. Post it. The world isn’t healed. It’s held. That’s enough.\n[L8] ________________\n[L9] \n[L10] \n[L11] Chapter 1: Wet Trace at Blackgate\n[L12] Bell Two rang short across the Underface. Jhace climbed the ladder out of the low heat, hand closing on rung, the metal sweating under his palm. He came up into Blackgate’s choke where the carts were backed nose to nose, and the Posting board glared white with its Tempermark pin and droplet icon.\n[L13] Tiffani had already chalked a half-circle behind them so the crowd couldn’t press too close. She stood in the ring’s gap, one hand on her Veil case, the other tracing light against the stone seam. “Hold your tongue out of the way,” she said without looking. “It’s a quick one.”\n[L14] Jhace set his pack down, rolled his sleeves, and touched the home ring bolted to the post. “One hand on home.”\n[L15] She nodded, voice gone flat with routine. “One hand on home.”\n[L16] Brighlee arrived from the Conclave, still breathing through paper. “Work order nine-three-two. Wet Trace, Blackgate span. Setter Jhace brast, glass Tiffani veld, no hold.” She Tempermarked the droplet card, clipped it to the board, and stepped back. Tiffani’s eyes lingered on the ink longer than Brighlee’s hand—counting strokes, weighing silence. Names posted, Bell recorded. The carts quieted.\n[L17] The note from the Chain said quick Vein under the gate plate—heat moving wrong, a shallow slip that could cut the cart path clean through the Underface if ignored. Persuasion before force. Always persuasion first.\n[L18] Jhace unpacked what he needed: two wedges, seven-degree cut; copper-nib trace stick; bladder of wet. Nothing else. He checked his fray bands and the dull brass ring on his left wrist for crack. Sound.\n[L19] Tiffani tilted the Lume rod, spreading its beam along the seam. The light came back too bright—bad depth.\n# 【3†The Line That Holds.txt†file_0000000056ec61f59aedbe23466069ae】\nContent source: Source.file\nTitle: The Line That Holds.txt\nCitation Marker: fileciteturn2file3\nMclick Target: \"2:3\"\nContent Snippet:\n[L1] “Quick vein wants the short path.”\n[L2] “Short path’s under their wheels,” he answered. “We give it a long one.”\n[L3] He took his wedges, set the first two spans north of the gate mouth. A low angle, shallow drive. The second he planted at the shoulder where the seam ducked under the bridge stone. Two measured taps. Wood met resistance, then held.\n[L4] “Half-beat Slake,” Tiffani said.\n[L5] He thumbed the bladder cap, wet the copper nib, flicked the bead clear. He placed it to the face and drew the line from north to shoulder, pressure through the shoulder, not the wrist. Wet Trace moved slow, steam rising in thin threads that curled before dying in the air. The smell was clean—mineral, no burn.\n[L6] Tiffani adjusted her light. “Shade three to four. Keep it honest.”\n[L7] “No white,” he said. He traced through the curve, kept the bead unbroken. A cart axle squealed behind them, then stopped when the driver saw the droplet card. A brake eased. The lane held.\n[L8] The copper scratched across grit. Jhace froze, steadied, smoothed on the second pass. The bead almost broke. He held his breath until it rejoined. Tiffani’s knuckles brushed his sleeve, steadied his wrist like truing a wheel.\n[L9] “Stay,” she said.\n[L10] He did. Her hand rested against his wrist, steadying the tremor. His muscles quieted.\n[L11] At the gate mouth, the Vein flicked toward the wheel groove. Veins liked edges; they remembered where stone met air. Jhace flattened the nib, widened the wet into a shallow bow across the lip. The Vein answered—a tight pulse running north. “Turning,” he said.\n[L12] “Counter it,” she said.\n[L13] He drew a narrow correction line upstream, heat balancing through stone. The trace shimmered, found the longer route, settled. The vein stopped tugging. Pressure equalized. Even breathing again.\n[L14] “Veil small,” she said. She warmed a palm-wide Shade skin, stretched it over the new trace, and tapped the edges in sevens, each strike exact. “Annealshift?”\n[L15] “Zero. Let the wall hold its own heat.”\n[L16] She nodded. “Veil in. Trace held.”\n[L17] Brighlee wrote the line as it cooled. “Wedge set, trace complete, Veil sealed. Bell two and three.”\n[L18] “Sign it,” Jhace said.\n[L19] She passed him the stamp. He pressed the setter mark into the metal plate beside the droplet symbol. The ring’s bite echoed down the stone.\n[L20] Tiffani leaned back, listening. “Gate’s steady. Field calm.”\n[L21] He touched the plate with his bare hand. Warm, not burning. “Field even,” he said. The heat moved out and down like a slow breath. “Cost: fray band worn, thirst.”\n[L22] She passed the bottle. Veld water always tasted faintly of glass. He drank and gave it back.\n[L23] “Policy,” she said. “Clinic if the ring hisses past four.”\n[L24] He grunted agreement. Brighlee clipped the finished work order under the droplet icon, lifted her ledger so the crowd could see the names. Tiffani’s chalk mark still hung half‑erased on the stone, a line left unfinished. The carts shifted. Law to motion again.\n[L25] Jhace crouched once more, checking the seam. Wet line dull and even. No bubbles under the veil, wedges seated clean. The air above the trace no longer shimmered.\n# 【4†The Line That Holds.txt†file_0000000056ec61f59aedbe23466069ae】\nContent source: Source.file\nTitle: The Line That Holds.txt\nCitation Marker: fileciteturn2file4\nMclick Target: \"2:4\"\nContent Snippet:\n[L1] The hiss stopped. Tiffani moved fast, laying two Shade 1 skins across the seam, sealing the new double brace. The water cooled; the air turned metallic and sweet.\n[L7] Brighlee recorded, clipped the interim slip, and stepped aside.\n[L8] Mel stood, brushing grit off her knees. “You saved it,” she said.\n[L9] “Temporarily.”\n[L10] “Nothing’s permanent.” She looked toward the queue. “Tell the carts they can pass, slow.”\n[L11] Tiffani lifted her Lume toward the post. “Witness?”\n[L12] Mel hesitated, hand above the ledger. “The policy’s new. This fix breaks it.”\n[L13] “Then mark it as precedent,” Jhace said.\n[L14] Mel studied the line another long moment, then nodded. “Witness.” She signed, slow and deliberate.\n[L15] The carts started rolling again, wheels creaking, drivers staring down at the fresh seal as they passed. The air changed pitch. Blue banners flared at every post from Bridgegate to the Vale, the signal that stopped carts and silenced every forge at once. HALT ORDER: STRUCTURAL RISK.\n[L29] Jhace reached the rise at a run, lungs raw, coat half‑soaked from the night before. The flag snapped above the street, light cutting through fog. A ten‑span arch in the rise had cracked. Half the Upper Market’s weight ran through that bridge.\n[L30] Tiffani stood with both hands braced on the guard rail, eyes on the fissure widening between plates. “It’s pulling apart along the seam. Two Veins, opposite vectors.”\n[L31] He knelt, tracing with his glove. The vibration hit his bones. “Feels like a mis‑thread in the Crown feed. Someone over‑bound it.”\n[L32] “Conclave techs said the same. They bailed.”\n[L33] “They left mid‑HALT?”\n[L34] “They said consultation complete.”\n[L35] “We’re it, then.”\n[L36] Brighlee’s voice carried from the post above. “Bell Five to Bell Nine window. Full HALT. No reopen without witness clearance. Work order three‑three‑eight.” She clipped the paper to the board; the crowd pulled back two meters on instinct.\n[L37] “Half the market’s watching,” Tiffani said.\n[L38] “Good,” Jhace said. “They can remember what this costs.”\n[L39] The crack ran three spans, straight and deep.\n# 【5†The Line That Holds.md†file_000000004ed061f5961349461f22bbdf】\nContent source: Source.file\nTitle: The Line That Holds.md\nCitation Marker: fileciteturn2file5\nMclick Target: \"2:5\"\nContent Snippet:\n[L1] Tempermark.  \n[L2] The Bore taught one rule that never stopped mattering: everything carries stress, and stress remembers. The skin tore with no stretch, like old paper. “Shade mark reads one,” she said, squinting at the faint stamp. “Lot L/P–43.”\n[L3] “Lonce & Parr,” Jhace said. “Crown supplier.”\n[L4] She nodded once. “We fix the seam first.”\n[L5] He set a wedge midline to quiet any wander, then thumbed the bladder and drew a short wet along the seam where the Veil had lifted. Half-beat Slake. Steam rose and vanished. The line took at once. No fault in the plate.\n[L6] Tiffani warmed a new Shade 1 from her kit—different stamp, a local mark—and laid it in with seven taps per edge. The lip sealed tight, no haze.\n[L7] “Test,” Jhace said.\n[L8] She ran the Lume along it. Light came back flat. “Set.” Her eyes went to the torn skin in her palm. “We’re not done.”\n[L9] He followed her gaze. “You think it’s wider?”\n[L10] “We check every Veil we laid yesterday near the Crown feeds.”\n[L11] He grimaced. “That’s eight sites.”\n[L12] “Better than losing a span.”\n[L13] They took Chalkway’s ladder up to the side run and crossed three corners where the pipes were numbered in old paint. At the second site, a Veil on the lower lip had bubbled like a blister. Tiffani cut it with her knife. The skin split along straight grain.\n[L14] “Same lot,” she said.\n[L15] Jhace swore softly. “Pulling it.”\n[L16] He wedged shallow, damped the seam, and Tiffani replaced the skin. They moved fast. At the third site, the Veil was intact but tacky to the touch.\n[L17] She tested the edge with a fingernail. The lip smeared. “Heat in storage,” she said. “Lonce & Parr kept it too close to a main.”\n[L18] “Post recall?”\n[L19] “Not yet. We need three marks.”\n[L20] By Bell Two they had five. Each failure carried the same tiny lot stamp under the corner curl: L/P–43. Tiffani logged the codes on a scrap. Brighlee wrote behind them without being asked, ink making small, precise sounds.\n[L21] At the sixth site a teamster waited with a handcart loaded with Crown-branded skins. “Delivery for Conclave stores,” he said.\n[L22] Tiffani didn’t answer. She cut a corner off the top skin. It tore like chalky bark.\n[L23] “Where from?” Jhace asked.\n[L24] “Lonce & Parr,” the teamster said, shifting like he knew he’d brought a problem to the wrong door.\n[L25] Tiffani held up the torn piece. “Take it back.”\n[L26] “I’m paid to deliver to store.”\n[L27] “Then you can tell them you weren’t allowed.”\n[L28] He glanced at Jhace. The Vein answered—a tight pulse running north. “Turning,” he said.  \n[L2] “Counter it,” she said.  \n[L3] He drew a narrow correction line upstream, heat balancing through stone. The trace shimmered, found the longer route, settled. The vein stopped tugging. Pressure equalized. Even breathing again.  \n[L4] “Veil small,” she said. The ring’s bite echoed down the stone.  \n[L10] Tiffani leaned back, listening. “Gate’s steady. Field calm.”  \n[L11] He touched the plate with his bare hand. The air above the trace no longer shimmered. “Blackgate’s quiet.”  \n[L16] Tiffani smiled without teeth, the kind of smile that left the ledger unbalanced. “It remembers when we make it look good.”  \n[L17] They packed in silence. Tools wiped, copper cooled, wedges tapped free. Brighlee closed her ledger with a single snap. The sound meant done.  \n[L18] The first cart eased forward, front wheel passing the seam. The rim rolled the shallow bow and stayed silent. The driver glanced down, then up, gave the small nod that meant you did the thing; I saw you.  \n[L19] They stayed until the third cart cleared, then unhooked from the home ring. Tiffani closed her case. Brighlee walked off, already writing the next line of work that would prove they’d lived this day correctly. Jhace lingered, eyes on the wet mark as it cooled. The steam had gone to thin breath, rising straight and vanishing against the stone.  \n[L20] \\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\n[L21] \n[L22] ## **Chapter 2: Thread Draw at Strathmoor Span**\n[L23] \n[L24] Bell Four came late, smothered by fog off the river. The air sat wet enough to drink. Jhace crossed the east truss walkway, his boots scraping the rust film that always rose before thaw. Strathmoor Span was a good bridge when it wanted to be—broad face, six weight lines—but it carried a habit of slow leaks under the mid-beam couplers.             "\n﻿Prologue — The Year the World Took a Breath\nThe world ended once and decided it was too much trouble to stay dead. It didn’t break apart; it flexed, like a lung taking air after being punched. A pull went through the crust—straight, fast, absolute—and stopped just short of tearing clean through. What it left was a tunnel with no opposite mouth. People called it the Bore, because naming the wound makes it sound finished.\nFrom the Upper Crown, it looks like an even circle of shadow on maps. From the Underface, it’s a black horizon that presses in your teeth when the air gets heavy. Nobody pretends it’s a mystery anymore. We live around it, not above it. Every crack, every bridge, every load-bearing inch answers to what the Bore changed.\nIt began with water taking new routes. Rivers turned, cliffs sagged, docks listed without warning. For a year the wind came up from the ground instead of the sky, and you could smell iron on your skin no matter how often you washed. People called it divine; the rest of us called it gravity. When the air stopped shaking, a handful of us were still standing, and we started measuring before we started praying.\nWe found the veins by accident. They ran under the ground like nerves under skin, thin lines where force preferred to travel. When the veins slipped out of their old paths, they bled heat and pressure and made Harrow—the kind of rupture that doesn’t care if you’re watching. A few people, tired of being erased, learned to touch the veins and guide them. Those hands became Veinwrights. Their work became the city’s language: Trace. Set. Bridge. Veil. Slake. Tempermark.\nThe Bore taught one rule that never stopped mattering: everything carries stress, and stress remembers. You can’t erase a fault; you can only give it a safer way to move. That’s what the craft is—negotiation between material and will. Every building stands because someone convinced it not to fall.\nSix months after the pull, the first bridges started breathing. At night you could see vapor lifting from the joints like ghost breath. No one remembers laying the mains that kept them warm, but the warmth stayed. It rose through basements and clinics, through pipes that had no valves, through the Conclave halls where the Veinwrights kept their ledgers. The city learned to live with the heat as a fact, not a gift. It kept people alive in winter, and it kept them honest—because if a line failed, everyone nearby heard it.\nWhen the air cooled, the Bells came. Not temple chimes—work signals. Long clear rings for reopen, two short for brace, fast beats for Harrow risk. Each Bell came with a board stamped in copper and sealed in glass. You could tell a city’s health by how clean its Tempermarks were.\nThe first posted rule was ugly and perfect: One hand on the home ring. Hold something that won’t move while you touch what might. It was less philosophy, more survival.\nThen came the rest, written by people who’d already bled once for the knowledge: — Trace wet. Dry lines please eyes and lie to Veins. — Wedge before Veil. Cool the draft, then the glass. — Half-beat Slake. — Countermark cooler than birth. Pride bends things wrong. — No White. — Brace taps only in Bells Two and Three. You are not special in Four. — If it isn’t on the board, it didn’t happen.\nThey’re not prayers. They’re methods. Watch a street when a blue HALT goes up and every hammer stops midair. Watch the crowd hold breath until the setter witness signs the clear. That’s how cities stay alive—by honoring pause more than noise.\nWe forbid Overbind, because a clean disaster still kills you. We forbid Whitequench, because a lie in glass cuts deeper than heat. We measure by what doesn’t fail, not by what shines.\nAfter the Bore, Bells multiplied. Every trade learned its rhythm. The Couriers’ Bell marked motion; the Conclave’s marked repair. You could walk a full day and never be out of hearing range. It was noise that meant survival—call, answer, repeat.\nSix hundred and twelve rounds later, Te’Oga still leans a fraction toward the Bore. Maps mark the tilt with a single diagonal line through the city’s name. Children in the Underface draw circles in ash to guess the next drift. Crown engineers add decimal places to comfort themselves. Neither side is wrong.\nThe Bore doesn’t threaten anymore. It just exists. We’ve made a kind of peace with the wound: keep it measured, keep it known, keep it held.\nWork here isn’t sacred. It’s necessary. The Conclave says “Trace wet.” The Couriers answer, “One hand on home.” Together, they make the city stay where it is.\nIf you need a prayer, you use your hands: Trace wet. Wedge before Veil. Slake on the half-beat. Tempermark what you promise. Post it. The world isn’t healed. It’s held. That’s enough.\n________________\n\n\nChapter 1: Wet Trace at Blackgate\nBell Two rang short across the Underface. Jhace climbed the ladder out of the low heat, hand closing on rung, the metal sweating under his palm. He came up into Blackgate’s choke where the carts were backed nose to nose, and the Posting board glared white with its Tempermark pin and droplet icon.\nTiffani had already chalked a half-circle behind them so the crowd couldn’t press too close. She stood in the ring’s gap, one hand on her Veil case, the other tracing light against the stone seam. “Hold your tongue out of the way,” she said without looking. “It’s a quick one.”\nJhace set his pack down, rolled his sleeves, and touched the home ring bolted to the post. “One hand on home.”\nShe nodded, voice gone flat with routine. “One hand on home.”\nBrighlee arrived from the Conclave, still breathing through paper. “Work order nine-three-two. Wet Trace, Blackgate span. Setter Jhace brast, glass Tiffani veld, no hold.” She Tempermarked the droplet card, clipped it to the board, and stepped back. Tiffani’s eyes lingered on the ink longer than Brighlee’s hand—counting strokes, weighing silence. Names posted, Bell recorded. The carts quieted.\nThe note from the Chain said quick Vein under the gate plate—heat moving wrong, a shallow slip that could cut the cart path clean through the Underface if ignored. Persuasion before force. Always persuasion first.\nJhace unpacked what he needed: two wedges, seven-degree cut; copper-nib trace stick; bladder of wet. Nothing else. He checked his fray bands and the dull brass ring on his left wrist for crack. Sound.\nTiffani tilted the Lume rod, spreading its beam along the seam. The light came back too bright—bad depth. She adjusted the Shade one mark darker until the glare steadied. “Fault’s running shallow,” she said. “Quick vein wants the short path.”\n“Short path’s under their wheels,” he answered. “We give it a long one.”\nHe took his wedges, set the first two spans north of the gate mouth. A low angle, shallow drive. The second he planted at the shoulder where the seam ducked under the bridge stone. Two measured taps. Wood met resistance, then held.\n“Half-beat Slake,” Tiffani said.\nHe thumbed the bladder cap, wet the copper nib, flicked the bead clear. He placed it to the face and drew the line from north to shoulder, pressure through the shoulder, not the wrist. Wet Trace moved slow, steam rising in thin threads that curled before dying in the air. The smell was clean—mineral, no burn.\nTiffani adjusted her light. “Shade three to four. Keep it honest.”\n“No white,” he said. He traced through the curve, kept the bead unbroken. A cart axle squealed behind them, then stopped when the driver saw the droplet card. A brake eased. The lane held.\nThe copper scratched across grit. Jhace froze, steadied, smoothed on the second pass. The bead almost broke. He held his breath until it rejoined. Tiffani’s knuckles brushed his sleeve, steadied his wrist like truing a wheel.\n“Stay,” she said.\nHe did. Her hand rested against his wrist, steadying the tremor. His muscles quieted.\nAt the gate mouth, the Vein flicked toward the wheel groove. Veins liked edges; they remembered where stone met air. Jhace flattened the nib, widened the wet into a shallow bow across the lip. The Vein answered—a tight pulse running north. “Turning,” he said.\n“Counter it,” she said.\nHe drew a narrow correction line upstream, heat balancing through stone. The trace shimmered, found the longer route, settled. The vein stopped tugging. Pressure equalized. Even breathing again.\n“Veil small,” she said. She warmed a palm-wide Shade skin, stretched it over the new trace, and tapped the edges in sevens, each strike exact. “Annealshift?”\n“Zero. Let the wall hold its own heat.”\nShe nodded. “Veil in. Trace held.”\nBrighlee wrote the line as it cooled. “Wedge set, trace complete, Veil sealed. Bell two and three.”\n“Sign it,” Jhace said.\nShe passed him the stamp. He pressed the setter mark into the metal plate beside the droplet symbol. The ring’s bite echoed down the stone.\nTiffani leaned back, listening. “Gate’s steady. Field calm.”\nHe touched the plate with his bare hand. Warm, not burning. “Field even,” he said. The heat moved out and down like a slow breath. “Cost: fray band worn, thirst.”\n"

            "You dropped the .txt. Good. You want sharp, you get sharp. Here’s a **tight, two-page prologue** you can paste in, plus **surgical notes** through Ch 13 so the book stops meandering and starts cutting. fileciteturn1file0\n\n# Prologue — The Year the World Took a Breath (compressed draft)\nThe world ended once and decided staying dead was too much work. A straight pull went through the crust, fast and absolute, then stopped short. It left a tunnel with no opposite mouth. We named the wound the **Bore** so it would pretend to be finished.\n\nFrom the Crown it’s a neat circle of map-shadow. From the Underface it’s a black horizon that hums against your teeth when the air gets heavy. Nobody calls it sacred now. We live around it. Every crack, bridge, and heartbeat answers to what the Bore changed.\n\nFirst the water learned new paths. Rivers turned. Cliffs sagged. Docks listed between breaths. For a year, wind came up from the ground, and iron lived on skin no matter how you scrubbed. People called it divine. The rest of us called it **gravity**. When the shaking quit, a few of us were still standing. We measured before we prayed.\n\nThat’s how we found the **veins**: thin routes where force prefers to travel. When veins slipped their old beds they bled heat and pressure and made **Harrow**, the kind of rupture that doesn’t care if you’re watching. A handful of stubborn hands learned to touch the veins and guide them. Those hands became **Veinwrights**. Our language is simple and paid for: **Trace. Set. Bridge. Veil. Slake. Tempermark.**\n\nThe Bore taught one rule that never stopped mattering: **everything carries stress, and stress remembers**. You don’t erase a fault. You give it a safer way to move. Every building stands because someone convinced it not to fall.\n\nSix months after the pull, the first bridges started breathing. At night, vapor lifted from the joints like ghost breath. No one remembers laying the mains that keep them warm, but the warmth stayed. It rose through basements and clinics, through pipes with no valves, through the Conclave halls where the ledgers live. We learned to treat heat as a fact, not a gift. When a line fails, the whole street hears it.\n\nThen came the **Bells**. Not temple chimes, work signals. Long clear ring to reopen; two short for brace; fast beats for Harrow risk. Each Bell hung near a board stamped in copper and sealed in glass. You can tell a city’s health by how clean its **Tempermarks** read.\n\nThe first posted rule was ugly and perfect: **One hand on the home ring.** Hold something that won’t move while you touch what might. The rest were written by people who already bled for the knowledge:\n\n- **Trace wet.** Dry lines please eyes and lie to veins.  \n- **Wedge before Veil.** Cool the draft, then the glass.  \n- **Half-beat Slake.**  \n- **Countermark cooler than birth.** Pride bends things wrong.  \n- **No White.**  \n- **Brace taps only in Bells Two and Three.** You are not special in Four.  \n- **If it isn’t on the board, it didn’t happen.**\n\nThey’re not prayers. They’re methods. Watch a street when a blue **HALT** goes up and every hammer stops midair. Watch the crowd hold breath until the witness signs the clear. That’s survival: honoring pause over noise.\n\nTwo things we forbid even when it would be pretty: **Overbind**, because a clean disaster still kills you; and **Whitequench**, because a lie in glass cuts deeper than heat.\n\nBells multiplied. Trades learned rhythms. You can walk a full day and stay in hearing. Noise means we’re still choosing one another.\n\nSix hundred and twelve rounds later, **Te’Oga** leans a fraction toward the Bore. Maps mark the tilt with a diagonal through the name. Children in the Underface draw ash circles to guess the next drift. Crown engineers add decimal places to comfort themselves. Neither side is wrong.\n\nThe Bore doesn’t threaten anymore; it exists. Peace means we keep it measured, known, and held.\n\nWork here isn’t sacred. It’s necessary. The Conclave says, “Trace wet.” The Couriers answer, “One hand on home.” That’s how the city stays where it is.\n\nIf you need a prayer, you use your hands: Trace wet. Wedge before Veil. Slake on the half-beat. Tempermark what you promise. Post it. **The world isn’t healed. It’s held.** That’s enough.\n\n---\n\n# Surgical notes by chapter (do this, not vibes)\n- **Prologue:** use the compressed draft above. It keeps the Bore, the Bells, the creed, and ban list. Dump the rest into short epigraphs at chapter heads.  \n- **Ch1: Wet Trace at Blackgate.** Strong opener. Cut a few redundant “home ring” echoes and let Tiffani steady Jhace once, not twice, so the intimacy lands harder. Trim 10%.  \n- **Ch2: Thread Draw at Strathmoor.** Good hand talk. The fog banter is the human glue; keep it. Add one tiny on-page cost (Tiffani’s palm blister pops when she taps the Veil) so wins aren’t free.  \n- **Ch3: Counterbend at Lowcourt Arch.** You flirt with catastrophe; consummate it. Let the first wedge slip and chip a bystander’s boot. Public consequences make later policy feel earned.  \n- **Ch4: Heat Splice under Alderline.** Great set piece. Name the upstream valve that “always sticks” so it can fail later on a schedule, not convenience.  \n- **Ch5: Lockfall at Greymantle Cut.** Visceral. Anchor space with 3 landmarks early so readers aren’t lost in steam: “stair, sluice gate, red pump.”  \n- **Ch6: Corlexi’s Fire (Interlude).** Perfect policy theater. Tag one skeptical teamster who reappears in Ch13 recognizing the new marks.  \n- **Ch7: Double Fault at Rindle Yard.** You finally admit the system itself is complicit. Good. Put a face on Lonce & Parr: have a company rep arrive late, try to shift blame, and get recorded.  \n- **Ch8: The HALT at Narrowvale Rise.** The “consultation complete” walk-off is infuriating in the right way. Write one Crown tech’s name. You need a human you can punish later.  \n- **Ch9: Slow Bell at Mirecourt.** Exhaustion’s creeping in. Put a micro-error on Tiffani that forces Mel to call a **mandatory clinic** on the page, not just in notes.  \n- **Ch10: Mobel at the Table (Interlude).** Chef’s kiss. Have him pocket one forged weight “for training” and melt it in public two chapters later.  \n- **Ch11: Batch Marks at Chalkway Sump.** This is your corporate smoking gun. Escalate: one L/P-43 skin fails mid-crowd so the recall isn’t abstract.  \n- **Ch12: Skew Line at Wains Cut.** The “shop trace” ban is excellent. Add a posted comparison card showing true wet vs cosmetic. Shaming works.  \n- **Ch13: Thirteen Corners.** Make it a rolling set piece with a clock. Each corner solved flips a lever that makes the next harder. No lateral victories.\n\n# Missing bruises (put pain on the page)\n- **Whitequench:** do a quick demo that looks perfect and later slices a kid’s boot. Make readers hate how pretty it was.  \n- **Overbind:** show a Crown-blessed overbind that holds until a temperature swing, then fails in a single, sick snap. That’s why the ban exists.\n\n# POV discipline\nClose third, one head per scene. Move your aphorisms into epigraphs posted on boards. No sudden omniscient fortune-cookie lines mid-action.\n\n# Antagonists with teeth\n- **Eddin Parr**, L&P logistics czar: too clean, never touches a tool, weaponizes “variance.”  \n- **Crown fixer**, name him, and let him “consult” during HALT then vanish. Bring him back for the inquiry.  \nTie both to a spreadsheet sin: heat-storage near mains to save rent, leading to L/P-43 delam. You already set the trap in Ch11–12. Spring it.\n\n# Micro line edits (punchier, same voice)\n- “People called it divine; the rest of us called it gravity.” → leave as is. It’s your thesis.  \n- “The smell was clean—mineral, no burn.” → “Clean mineral, no burn.”  \n- “The driver glanced down, then up, gave the small nod…” → “The driver glanced down, up, then gave the nod that means: you did the thing; I saw you.”  \n- “You’re an idiot.” / “Functional idiot.” → keep. It finally lets them breathe.\n\n# Continuity and pacing to fix\n- **Bell math:** map each job to exact Bell windows; no hand-wavy “half.”  \n- **Costs that stick:** Jhace’s hand changes technique later. Tiffani’s fog-sickness forces delegation once. Mel signs one fix she can’t fully prove and lives with it.  \n- **Posted consequences:** any rule-break hits a board within two chapters, changed behavior on the street.\n\n# Title and logline, tuned\n- Keep **The Line That Holds**. It earns itself.  \n- Logline: *When a city built over a one-mouthed abyss starts to drift, a crew of Veinwrights must break their posted rules to keep bridges breathing as a supplier’s quiet sabotage turns safety into theater and faith into math.*\n\n# Punch-list you can knock out this week\n1) Swap in the compressed Prologue.  \n2) Name one Crown tech and one L&P exec. Put them on-page twice.  \n3) Add Whitequench and Overbind demos with visible harm.  \n4) Make Ch13 a timed cascade.  \n5) Add three posted-rule epigraphs; cut omniscient asides.  \n6) Seed a single repeating landmark system so readers always know where the body is in the city.  \n7) Ensure clinic slips are enforced once, not threatened.  \n8) Give Corlexi and Mobel outcomes that force plot changes, not just vibes.  \n9) Lock Bell timing to an outline.  \n10) Post every policy shift on the board, then show behavior changing.\n\nThis thing already smokes. Trim the sermon, raise the price of every win, and let the city bruise. Then it’ll stick to readers’ ribs like a hard truth with heat behind it. fileciteturn1file0"

            "You want full research on your prose and stakes, then a paste-ready prompt your custom GPT can execute. Fine. Here’s the read, then the tool to do the surgery.\n\n# Prose & Stakes: what the text is actually doing\n\n## Prose DNA (what’s on the page)\n- **Workmanlike lyricism.** Short, declarative lines built from physical actions, with just enough image to sting. Example cadence sits right in the open: “People called it divine; the rest of us called it gravity.” fileciteturn2file1L4-L5\n- **Diegetic craft lexicon.** The book teaches through doing: Trace, Veil, Slake, Tempermark, posted rules. It’s not lore-dump for the sake of it; characters enact it on the job. fileciteturn2file1L5-L10\n- **Close third that hugs hands and tools.** Action is tactile and procedural: wedge angle, bead behavior, steam threads, finger pressure. fileciteturn3file2L4-L11\n- **Public ritual as voice device.** HALT order, boards, bells, witness signature. This keeps scenes civic, not just personal. fileciteturn3file4L1-L2\n- **Sermon lines used sparingly, better when anchored to policy.** “If it isn’t on the board, it didn’t happen.” lands because it governs what we see signed and posted. fileciteturn2file1L10-L11\n\n## Stakes Map (where danger really comes from)\n- **Civic stakes (crowd, city, infrastructure).** HALT freezes an entire market; reopen requires a witnessed clear. The human sea watching adds pressure you can hear. fileciteturn2file4L28-L37\n- **Systemic stakes (bad materials, policy, supply chain).** Lonce & Parr lot L/P-43 fails in the field; you escalate to a recall with on-street proof and a formal quarantine. That’s plot, not flavor. fileciteturn3file0L4-L8 fileciteturn3file0L21-L28\n- **Institutional friction (dereliction by “experts”).** Crown techs “consultation complete” then bail mid-HALT. Smart infuriating beat. fileciteturn2file4L31-L36\n- **Personal stakes (body cost).** Jhace’s torn palm and clinic policy aren’t props; they change how he can work and when. Use that later as a constraint. fileciteturn2file4L16-L21\n- **Temporal stakes (Bell windows).** Jobs run against Bells; reopen is not vibes, it’s a clock. Keep exploiting this. fileciteturn2file4L36-L39\n\n## Where stakes still sag\n- **Banned methods are named, not dramatized.** We see the rules against Overbind/Whitequench, and one suspected overbind, but not a visceral on-page demonstration with fallout. Add two concise, echoing set-pieces. fileciteturn3file4L1-L2 fileciteturn2file4L31-L34\n- **Antagonism is mostly corporate/systemic, not personal.** L/P exists, but the human face of that malice shows up only in logistics beats. You’ll get more voltage if one executive and one Crown fixer recur at the scene level. fileciteturn3file0L21-L28\n- **Job loop predictability still pokes through.** The craft is compelling, but some scenes resolve cleanly after the same “arrive-fix-sign” rhythm. Keep the rhythm; vary the cost and the shape of the failure.\n\n---\n\n# Paste-ready prompt for your custom GPT\n\n> Use this whole block as the single system prompt for your model. It’s surgical and strict by design.\n\n```\nROLE\nYou are a senior line editor and structural surgeon for an engineered-fantasy novel. Your job: tighten prose without bleaching voice, and raise stakes without melodrama. Operate scene by scene. Never introduce lore; prove it through action, policy, and consequences.\n\nINPUTS\n1) Full manuscript text.\n2) This style sheet and world rules (enforce, don’t overwrite):\n   - Caps: Bore, Bells, Vein, Veinwright, Conclave, Crown, Underface, Trace, Veil, Slake, Tempermark, HALT.\n   - Tools lower: wedges, shade skins (but “Shade 1/2” as grade stays capped), copper nib, Lume.\n   - Mantras/rules may be italicized on first use in a scene only.\n   - POV: close third, one head per scene. No omniscient aphorisms inside action.\n   - Bell math must be consistent and auditable on the page.\n   - If it isn’t on the board, it didn’t happen.\n\nOUTPUT FORMAT\n- For each chapter, produce:\n  A) “CHANGELOG” (bullet list, 5–12 items): concrete edits and why.\n  B) “REWRITE” section: the revised chapter text.\n  C) “CHECKS”: a short checklist confirming POV, Bell window, public/witness consequence, and cost.\n- Use minimally invasive rewrites: keep paragraphing when possible. Cut repetition. Do not add new POVs.\n- Mark any added epigraph with: [EPIGRAPH]…[/EPIGRAPH].\n- When you seed a new antagonist or policy detail, tag the first occurrence with [SEED]…[/SEED] and use it again at least twice in later chapters.\n\nGLOBAL GOALS\n1) **Tighten Prose**\n   - Cut redundancy and exposition that restates already-shown facts.\n   - Replace adjectives with concrete action or sensory detail.\n   - Keep the craft lexicon. Show technique through hands, tools, heat, weight.\n2) **Escalate Stakes**\n   - Every scene must pay at least one of these costs:\n     • Body: injury, exhaustion, loss of tool/material.\n     • Policy: a posted variance, a clinic order, or a witnessed precedent.\n     • Time: a Bell window compressing work or forcing triage.\n     • Civic: crowd pressure, commerce halted, public risk.\n   - Scale costs forward: if an injury or variance occurs, constrain options in at least two future scenes.\n3) **Antagonist Pressure**\n   - Introduce two named recurring opponents:\n     • Lonce & Parr executive (clean hands, dirty ledgers).\n     • Crown “consultant” who bails during HALT.\n   - They must appear on-page at least twice each, speaking or acting, and cause a concrete complication (delay, bad lot, policy trap).\n4) **Demonstrate the Forbidden**\n   - Add two compact, high-clarity set-pieces:\n     • WHITEQUENCH DEMO: a gorgeous, wrong quench that later fails and injures a named bystander. Show sound, texture, and the delayed snap. Post the recall on-page.\n     • OVERBIND DEMO: a “holds perfectly” fix that catastrophically fails with a temperature swing. Show why “a clean disaster still kills you.”\n   - Each must ripple forward into policy and behavior changes (boards updated, clinic orders, storage or inspection protocols).\n5) **Epigraphs (OPTIONAL)**\n   - If EPIGRAPHS=ON, prepend each chapter with 1–2 lines as posted rules or Bell codes tied to the scene’s work order. Keep them diegetic, not poetic.\n\nPROCESS (PER CHAPTER)\n1) DIAGNOSE: list bloat, repeated beats, vague antagonism, weak cost.\n2) BELL & POLICY: explicitly set the Bell window; identify board marks; ensure a witness moment or explain absence.\n3) PROSE PASS: compress 10–20% by removing duplication, tightening verbs, and cutting sermon lines unless they’re posted rules.\n4) STAKES PASS: inject or escalate at least one cost. If a rule is broken, show the consequence inside 1–2 chapters (clinic slip, variance post, audit).\n5) ANTAG/DEMO PASS: where appropriate, thread in L&P exec or Crown fixer. Place WHITEQUENCH/OVERBIND demos at planned slots without derailing continuity.\n6) CONTINUITY: propagate injuries, tool loss, or policy changes forward. Update Bell math consistently.\n7) FINALIZE: produce CHANGELOG, REWRITE, CHECKS.\n\nSUCCESS CRITERIA (VERIFY)\n- Prologue trimmed to ~600–800 words while preserving Bore, Bells, credo, ban list.\n- Each chapter contains at least one explicit cost (Body/Policy/Time/Civic).\n- Banned methods appear once each with visible harm and follow-through.\n- Two named antagonists recur and materially worsen the team’s options.\n- No omniscient intrusions; all wisdom moves to posted rules/boards.\n- Bell windows, witness signatures, and postings are consistent and obvious.\n\nKNOBS\n- EPIGRAPHS: ON|OFF (default OFF)\n- COMPRESSION_TARGET: percentage per chapter (default 12%)\n- MAX_NEW_TEXT_PER_CHAPTER: words (default 250)\n- TONE_GUARDRAIL: “workmanlike, unsentimental, tactile; no purple”\n\nEXAMPLES (TEMPLATES, NOT CONTENT)\n[EPIGRAPH] Trace wet. Wedge before Veil. — Board: Blackgate Span, Bell Two [/EPIGRAPH]\n\nCHECKS example:\n- POV: close third (Jhace) ✅\n- Bell window: 2–3 ✅\n- Consequence: clinic order posted ✅\n- Public: witness signature on board ✅\n\nDO NOTS\n- Do not add new magic systems or cosmology.\n- Do not break the rule vocabulary or capitalization standards.\n- Do not shift to omniscient mid-scene.\n- Do not add quips; humor must come from work reality and policy friction.\n```\n\nThat prompt will make your model do the boring, necessary work and keep your voice intact while actually ratcheting tension.
